## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task involves the rate of change of concentration (dA/dt) as a function of time and concentration A, which is a classic chemical kinetics problem. The rate law typically relates dA/dt to powers of concentration A, and may involve time-dependent terms for complex reaction mechanisms.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- {'name': 'Zero-order kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0', 'scenario': 'Reaction rate independent of concentration'}
- {'name': 'First-order kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A', 'scenario': 'Rate proportional to concentration (radioactive decay, simple decomposition)'}
- {'name': 'Second-order kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A**2', 'scenario': 'Rate proportional to square of concentration (bimolecular reaction)'}
- {'name': 'nth-order kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A**c1', 'scenario': 'General power-law rate expression for arbitrary reaction order'}
- {'name': 'Mixed-order kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2', 'scenario': 'Competing first and second order pathways'}
- {'name': 'Reversible first-order kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A + c1', 'scenario': 'First-order reaction with reverse reaction or constant production term'}
- {'name': 'Saturation kinetics (Michaelis-Menten-like)', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A / (A + c1)', 'scenario': 'Enzyme or catalytic reaction with substrate saturation'}
- {'name': 'Inhibition kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A**2)', 'scenario': 'Substrate inhibition in enzyme kinetics'}
- {'name': 'Autocatalytic reaction', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A)', 'scenario': 'Autocatalytic process where product catalyzes the reaction'}
- {'name': 'Time-dependent exponential decay rate', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t)', 'scenario': 'Rate that follows exponential time dependence directly'}
- {'name': 'Polynomial rate with time', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * t', 'scenario': 'Rate depending on both concentration and explicit time'}
- {'name': 'Power-law with time modulation', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 * exp(c2 * t)', 'scenario': 'Temperature-programmed or time-varying conditions'}
- {'name': 'Consecutive reaction intermediate', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) + c2 * exp(c3 * t)', 'scenario': 'Intermediate species in consecutive A→B→C reactions'}

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Negative rate of change (consumption) → dA_dt typically has a negative leading coefficient times positive powers of A
- Integer reaction order → Power of A is often 0, 1, 2, or 3 corresponding to molecularity of elementary steps
- Concentration approaching equilibrium → Rate expression includes (A - A_eq) terms or constant offsets
- Autocatalytic behavior (S-shaped concentration curves) → Product of A and (constant - A) terms in rate law
- Substrate inhibition (rate decreasing at high concentration) → A in numerator with A² in denominator of rational expression
- Parallel competing reactions → Sum of multiple power-law terms with different orders
- If dA/dt depends only on A (autonomous ODE) → time variable t should not appear explicitly in rate law
- Fractional reaction orders → Non-integer power c in A**c, often arising from complex mechanisms or surface reactions
